      <p>
       <b>
        The history of the Philippines from 1521 to 1898
       </b>
       , also known as the
       <b>
        Spanish Colonial Period,
       </b>
       began with the arrival in 1521 of European explorer
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
        Ferdinand Magellan
       </a>
       sailing for
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       , which heralded the period when the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       was a colony of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       , and ended with the outbreak of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       in 1898, which marked the beginning of the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)" title="History of the Philippines (1898–1946)">
        American Colonial Era
       </a>
       of Philippine history.
      </p>
      <div class="toc" id="toc">
       <div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en">
        <h2>
         Contents
        </h2>
       </div>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_expeditions_and_colonization">
        Spanish expeditions and colonization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Spanish expeditions and colonization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:186px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Magellan_(Retouched).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="448" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/184px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/276px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/368px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg 2x" width="184"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Magellan_(Retouched).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
          Ferdinand Magellan
         </a>
         arrived in the Philippines on March 16, 1521. When European traders in search for a new route to the Spice Islands, stumbled into the
         <b>
          Philippines.
         </b>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although the archipelago may have been visited before by the Portuguese (who conquered
       <a href="/wiki/Malacca_City" title="Malacca City">
        Malacca City
       </a>
       in 1511 and reached
       <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
        Maluku Islands
       </a>
       in 1512, the earliest documented European expedition to the Philippines was that led by
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
        Ferdinand Magellan
       </a>
       , in the service of the king of Spain. The expedition first sighted the mountains of
       <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">
        Samar
       </a>
       at dawn on the 16th March 1521, making landfall the following day at the small, uninhabited island of
       <a href="/wiki/Homonhon" title="Homonhon">
        Homonhon
       </a>
       at the mouth of the
       <a href="/wiki/Leyte_Gulf" title="Leyte Gulf">
        Leyte Gulf
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On Easter Sunday, 31 March 1521, at Limasawa Island, Southern Leyte, as is stated in
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Pigafetta" title="Antonio Pigafetta">
        Antonio Pigafetta
       </a>
       's Primo Viaggio Intorno El Mondo (First Voyage Around the World), Magellan solemnly planted a cross on the summit of a hill overlooking the sea and claimed for the king of Spain possession of the islands he had seen, naming them
       <i>
        Archipelago of Saint Lazarus
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Magellan conquered and sought alliances among the natives beginning with Datu Zula, the chieftain of Sugbu (now
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">
        Cebu
       </a>
       ), and took special pride in converting them to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">
        Catholicism
       </a>
       . Magellan's expedition got involved in the political rivalries between the Cebuano natives and took part in a battle against Lapu-lapu, chieftain of
       <a href="/wiki/Mactan" title="Mactan">
        Mactan island
       </a>
       and a mortal enemy of Datu Zula. At dawn on 27 April 1521,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mactan" title="Battle of Mactan">
        Magellan invaded Mactan Island
       </a>
       with 60 armed men and 1,000 Cebuano warriors, but had great difficulty landing his men on the rocky shore. Lapu-Lapu had an army of 1,500 on land. Magellan waded ashore with his soldiers and attacked the Mactan defenders, ordering Datu Zula and his warriors to remain aboard the ships and watch. Magellan seriously underestimated Lapu-Lapu and his men, and grossly outnumbered, Magellan and 14 of his soldiers were killed. The rest managed to reboard the ships.
      </p>
      <p>
       The battle left the expedition with too few crewmen to man three ships, so they abandoned the "Concepción". The remaining ships - "Trinidad" and "Victoria" – sailed to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spice_Islands" title="Spice Islands">
        Spice Islands
       </a>
       in present-day Indonesia. From there, the expedition split into two groups. The
       <i>
        Trinidad
       </i>
       , commanded by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gonzalo_G%C3%B3mez_de_Espinoza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gonzalo Gómez de Espinoza (page does not exist)">
        Gonzalo Gómez de Espinoza
       </a>
       tried to sail eastward across the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">
        Isthmus of Panama
       </a>
       . Disease and shipwreck disrupted Espinoza's voyage and most of the crew died. Survivors of the
       <i>
        Trinidad
       </i>
       returned to the Spice Islands, where the Portuguese imprisoned them. The
       <i>
        Victoria
       </i>
       continued sailing westward, commanded by
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastián Elcano">
        Juan Sebastián Elcano
       </a>
       , and managed to return to
       <a href="/wiki/Sanl%C3%BAcar_de_Barrameda" title="Sanlúcar de Barrameda">
        Sanlúcar de Barrameda
       </a>
       , Spain in 1522. In 1529,
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Charles I of Spain
       </a>
       relinquished all claims to the Spice Islands to
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       in the treaty of Zaragoza. However, the treaty did not stop the colonization of the Philippine archipelago from
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After Magellan's voyage, subsequent expeditions were dispatched to the islands. Five expeditions were sent: that of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garc%C3%ADa_Jofre_de_Loa%C3%ADsa" title="García Jofre de Loaísa">
        Loaisa
       </a>
       (1525),
       <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Cabot_(explorer)" title="Sebastian Cabot (explorer)">
        Cabot
       </a>
       (1526),
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Saavedra_Cer%C3%B3n" title="Álvaro de Saavedra Cerón">
        Saavedra
       </a>
       (1527),
       <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy López de Villalobos">
        Villalobos
       </a>
       (1542), and
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">
        Legazpi
       </a>
       (1564).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zaide2006pp86-87_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-zaide2006pp86-87-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Legazpi expedition was the most successful as it resulted in the discovery of the
       <i>
        tornaviaje
       </i>
       or return trip to Mexico across the Pacific by
       <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Urdaneta" title="Andrés de Urdaneta">
        Andrés de Urdaneta
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This discovery started the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleons" title="Manila Galleons">
        Manila galleon
       </a>
       trade, which lasted two and a half centuries.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4022" data-file-width="3474" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/152px-Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/228px-Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/304px-Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="152"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Titian_-_King_Philip_II_of_Spain_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Las Islas Filipinas was name after
         <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
          Philip II of Spain
         </a>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy López de Villalobos">
          Ruy López de Villalobos
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1543,
       <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy López de Villalobos">
        Ruy López de Villalobos
       </a>
       named the islands of Leyte and Samar
       <i>
        Las Islas Filipinas
       </i>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        Philip II of Spain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Philip II became King of Spain on January 16, 1556, when his father, Charles I of Spain, abdicated the Spanish throne. Philip was in
       <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">
        Brussels
       </a>
       at the time and his return to Spain was delayed until 1559 because of European politics and wars in northern Europe. Shortly after his return to Spain, Philip ordered an expedition mounted to the Spice Islands, stating that its purpose was "to discover the islands to the west". In reality its task was to conquer the Philippines for Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 19 or 20, 1564 a Spanish expedition of a mere 500 men led by
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">
        Miguel López de Legazpi
       </a>
       departed
       <a href="/wiki/Barra_de_Navidad" title="Barra de Navidad">
        Barra de Navidad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       , arriving off
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">
        Cebu
       </a>
       on February 13, 1565, conquering it despite Cebuano opposition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halili2004_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-halili2004-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA77" rel="nofollow">
          77
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1569, Legazpi transferred to
       <a href="/wiki/Panay" title="Panay">
        Panay
       </a>
       and founded a second settlement on the bank of the
       <a href="/wiki/Panay_River" title="Panay River">
        Panay River
       </a>
       . In 1570, Legazpi sent his grandson,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Salcedo" title="Juan de Salcedo">
        Juan de Salcedo
       </a>
       , who had arrived from Mexico in 1567, to
       <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">
        Mindoro
       </a>
       to punish the Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">
        Moro
       </a>
       pirates who had been plundering Panay villages. Salcedo also destroyed forts on the islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Ilin_Island" title="Ilin Island">
        Ilin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lubang_Island" title="Lubang Island">
        Lubang
       </a>
       , respectively South and Northwest of Mindoro.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halili2004_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-halili2004-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA79" rel="nofollow">
          79
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1570,
       <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_de_Goiti" title="Martín de Goiti">
        Martín de Goiti
       </a>
       , having been dispatched by Legazpi to Luzon, conquered the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Maynila" title="Kingdom of Maynila">
        Kingdom of Maynila
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       ), a puppet-state of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Brunei" title="Sultanate of Brunei">
        Sultanate of Brunei
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halili2004_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-halili2004-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gUt5v8ET4QYC&amp;pg=PA79" rel="nofollow">
          79
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       Legazpi then made Maynila the capital of the Philippines and simplified its spelling to
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       . His expedition also renamed
       <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">
        Luzon
       </a>
       <i>
        Nueva Castilla
       </i>
       . Legazpi became the country's first governor-general. With time, Cebu's importance fell as power shifted north to Luzon. The archipelago was Spain's outpost in the orient and Manila became the capital of the entire
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spanish East Indies
       </a>
       . The colony was administered through the Viceroyalty of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       (now Mexico) until 1821 when
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       achieved independence from Spain. After 1821, the colony was governed directly from Spain.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Lopez_de_Legazpi.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="233" data-file-width="170" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Miguel_Lopez_de_Legazpi.jpg/140px-Miguel_Lopez_de_Legazpi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/02/Miguel_Lopez_de_Legazpi.jpg 1.5x" width="140"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Lopez_de_Legazpi.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">
          Miguel López de Legazpi
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During most of the colonial period, the Philippine economy depended on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleons" title="Manila Galleons">
        Galleon Trade
       </a>
       which was inaugurated in 1565 between
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">
        Acapulco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       . Trade between Spain and the Philippines was via the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       to Mexico (
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">
        Acapulco
       </a>
       ), and then across the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       to Spain (
       <a href="/wiki/Veracruz_(city)" title="Veracruz (city)">
        Veracruz
       </a>
       to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cadiz" title="Cadiz">
        Cádiz
       </a>
       ). Manila became the most important center of trade in Asia between the 17th and 18th centuries. All sorts of products from
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">
        Brunei
       </a>
       , the Moluccas and even
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       were sent to Manila to be sold for silver 8-Real coins which came aboard the galleons from Acapulco. These goods, including
       <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">
        silk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Porcelain" title="Porcelain">
        porcelain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">
        spices
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lacquerware" title="Lacquerware">
        lacquerware
       </a>
       and textile products were then sent to Acapulco and from there to other parts of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       and Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       The European population in the archipelago steadily grew although natives remained the majority. During the initial period of colonization, Manila was settled by 1200 Spanish families.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">
        Cebu City
       </a>
       , at the Visayas, the settlement received a total of 2,100 soldier-settlers from
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       (Mexico).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the immediate south of Manila, Mexicans were present at Ermita
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and at
       <a href="/wiki/Cavite_City" title="Cavite City">
        Cavite
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       where they were stationed as sentries. In addition, men conscripted from
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       , were also sent to settle
       <a href="/wiki/Zamboanga_City" title="Zamboanga City">
        Zamboanga City
       </a>
       in Mindanao, to wage war upon Muslim pirates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were also communities of Spanish-Mestizos that developed in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaro,_Iloilo" title="Jaro, Iloilo">
        Iloilo
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Negros_Island" title="Negros Island">
        Negros
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vigan" title="Vigan">
        Vigan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IlocosHeritage_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IlocosHeritage-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Interactions between native Filipinos and immigrant Spaniards plus Latin-Americans eventually caused the formation of a new language,
       <a href="/wiki/Chavacano" title="Chavacano">
        Chavacano
       </a>
       , a creole of
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">
        Mexican Spanish
       </a>
       .They depended on the Galleon Trade for a living. In the later years of the 18th century, Governor-General Basco introduced economic reforms that gave the colony its first significant internal source income from the production of
       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">
        tobacco
       </a>
       and other agricultural exports. In this later period, agriculture was finally opened to the European population, which before was reserved only for the natives.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:336px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG/334px-SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG/501px-SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG/668px-SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG 2x" width="334"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SanAgustinManilajf4977_08.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tomb of
         <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">
          Miguel López de Legazpi
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila)" title="San Agustin Church (Manila)">
          San Agustin Church (Manila)
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">
          Intramuros
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During Spain’s 333 year rule in the Philippines, the colonists had to fight off the Chinese pirates (who lay siege to Manila, the most famous of which was
       <a href="/wiki/Limahong" title="Limahong">
        Limahong
       </a>
       in 1574),
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Dutch
       </a>
       forces,
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       forces, and indigenous revolts.
       <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">
        Moros
       </a>
       from western Mindanao and the Sulu Archipelago also raided the coastal Christian areas of Luzon and the Visayas and occasionally captured men and women to be sold as slaves.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some Japanese ships visited the Philippines in the 1570s in order to export Japanese
       <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">
        silver
       </a>
       and import Philippine
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       . Later, increasing imports of silver from New World sources resulted in Japanese exports to the Philippines shifting from silver to consumer goods. In the 1580s, the Spanish traders were troubled to some extent by Japanese pirates, but peaceful trading relations were established between the Philippines and Japan by 1590.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Japan's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kampaku" title="Kampaku">
        kampaku
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">
        regent
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyoshi" title="Toyotomi Hideyoshi">
        Toyotomi Hideyoshi
       </a>
       , demanded unsuccessfully on several occasions that the Philippines submit to Japan's
       <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">
        suzerainty
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 8, 1597, King
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        Philip II
       </a>
       , near the end of his 42-year reign, issued a
       <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">
        Royal Cedula
       </a>
       instructing
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Tello_de_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Francisco de Tello de Guzmán">
        Francisco de Tello de Guzmán
       </a>
       , then
       <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">
        Governor-General of the Philippines
       </a>
       to fulfill the laws of tributes and to provide for restitution of ill-gotten taxes taken from the natives. The decree was published in Manila on August 5, 1598. King Philip died on 13 September, just forty days after the publication of the decree, but his death was not known in the Philippines until middle of 1599, by which time a referendum by which the natives would acknowledge Spanish rule was underway. With the completion of the Philippine referendum of 1599, Spain could be said to have established legitimate sovereignty over the Philippines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_control">
        Spanish control
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Spanish control">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_the_Philippines" title="Captaincy General of the Philippines">
        Captaincy General of the Philippines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spanish East Indies
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">
        Political system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:255px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG/253px-The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG/380px-The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG/506px-The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG 2x" width="253"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Fort_San_Pedro.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Pedro" title="Fort San Pedro">
          Fort San Pedro
         </a>
         was first of the many fortress to protect the islands from the Invaders such as Pirates and other Colonizers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Spanish quickly organized their new colony according to their model. The first task was the reduction, or relocation of native inhabitants into settlements. The earliest political system used during the
       <i>
        conquista
       </i>
       period was the
       <i>
        encomienda
       </i>
       system, which resembled the feudal system in medieval Europe. The conquistadores, friars and native nobles were granted estates, in exchange for their services to the King, and were given the privilege to collect tribute from its inhabitants. In return, the person granted the
       <i>
        encomienda
       </i>
       , known as an
       <i>
        encomendero
       </i>
       , was tasked to provide military protection to the inhabitants, justice and governance. In times of war, the
       <i>
        encomendero
       </i>
       was duty bound to provide soldiers for the King, in particular, for the complete defense of the colony from invaders such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">
        Dutch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">
        British
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">
        Chinese
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        encomienda
       </i>
       system was abused by
       <i>
        encomenderos
       </i>
       and by 1700 was largely replaced by administrative provinces, each headed by an
       <i>
        alcalde mayor
       </i>
       (provincial governor)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most prominent feature of Spanish cities was the plaza, a central area for town activities such as the fiesta, and where government buildings, the church, a market area and other infrastructures were located. Residential areas lay around the plaza. During the
       <i>
        conquista
       </i>
       , the first task of colonization was the reduction, or relocation of the indigenous population into settlements surrounding the plaza.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_government">
        National government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: National government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       On the national level or social class, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" title="King of Spain">
        King of Spain
       </a>
       , via his
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Indies" title="Council of the Indies">
        Council of the Indies
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Consejo de las Indias
       </i>
       ), governed through his
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:241px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="782" data-file-width="980" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg/239px-Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg/359px-Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg/478px-Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg 2x" width="239"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chopsticks_in_the_Philippines.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chinese settlers in the Philippines
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       representative in the Philippines, the
       <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">
        Governor-General of the Philippines
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Gobernador y Capitán General
       </i>
       ). With the seat of power in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intramuros,_Manila" title="Intramuros, Manila">
        Intramuros, Manila
       </a>
       , the Governor-General was given several duties: head of the supreme court, the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Audiencia_of_Manila" title="Royal Audiencia of Manila">
         Royal Audiencia of Manila
        </a>
       </i>
       ; Commander-in-chief of the army and navy, and the economic planner of the country.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       All executive power of the local government stemmed from him and as
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">
        regal patron
       </a>
       , he had the authority to supervise mission work and oversee
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical" title="Ecclesiastical">
        ecclesiastical
       </a>
       appointments. His yearly salary was 40,000 pesos. The Governor-General was commonly a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Peninsulars" title="Peninsulars">
         peninsular Spaniard
        </a>
       </i>
       , a Spaniard born in Spain, to ensure loyalty of the colony to the
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:313px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1096" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png/311px-A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png/467px-A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png/622px-A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png 2x" width="311"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Hydrographical_and_Chorographical_Chart_of_the_Philippine_Islands_WDL10089.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Philippine map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       crown or tiara.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_government">
        Provincial government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Provincial government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Philippines" title="Provinces of the Philippines">
        Provinces of the Philippines
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On the local level, heading the pacified provinces (
       <i>
        alcaldia
       </i>
       ), was the provincial governor (
       <i>
        alcalde mayor
       </i>
       ). The unpacified military zones (
       <i>
        corregimiento
       </i>
       ), such as
       <a href="/wiki/Mariveles,_Bataan" title="Mariveles, Bataan">
        Mariveles
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">
        Mindoro
       </a>
       , were headed by the
       <i>
        corregidores
       </i>
       . City governments (
       <i>
        ayuntamientos
       </i>
       ), were also headed by an
       <i>
        alcalde mayor
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Alcalde mayors
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        corregidores
       </i>
       exercised multiple prerogatives as judge, inspector of
       <i>
        encomiendas
       </i>
       , chief of police, tribute collector, capitan-general of the province and even vice-regal patron. His annual salary ranged from P300 to P2000 before 1847 and P1500 to P1600 after it. But this can be augmented through the special privilege of "
       <i>
        indulto de commercio
       </i>
       " where all people were forced to do business with him. The
       <i>
        alcalde mayor
       </i>
       was usually an
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       (Spaniard born in the Philippines). In the 19th century, the
       <i>
        Peninsulares
       </i>
       began to displace the
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       which resulted in the political unrests of 1872, notably the execution of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GOMBURZA" title="GOMBURZA">
        GOMBURZA
       </a>
       , Novales Revolt and mutiny of the Cavite fort under La Madrid.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_government">
        Municipal government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Municipal government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        pueblo
       </i>
       or town is headed by the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gobernadorcillo" title="Gobernadorcillo">
         Gobernadorcillo
        </a>
       </i>
       or little governor. Among his administrative duties were the preparation of the tribute list (
       <i>
        padron
       </i>
       ), recruitment and distribution of men for draft labor, communal public work and military conscription (quinto), postal clerk and judge in minor civil suits. He intervened in all administrative cases pertaining to his town: lands, justice, finance and the municipal police. His annual salary, however, was only P24 but he was exempted from taxation. Any native or Chinese mestizo, 25 years old, literate in oral or written
      </p>
      <p>
       Any member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Principal%C3%ADa" title="Principalía">
        Principalía
       </a>
       , who speaks or who has knowledge of the Spanish language and has been a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cabeza_de_Barangay" title="Cabeza de Barangay">
         Cabeza de Barangay
        </a>
       </i>
       of 4 years can be a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gobernadorcillo" title="Gobernadorcillo">
         Gobernadorcillo
        </a>
       </i>
       . Among those prominent is
       <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">
        Emilio Aguinaldo
       </a>
       , a Chinese Mestizo and who was the
       <i>
        Gobernadorcillo
       </i>
       of Cavite El Viejo (now
       <a href="/wiki/Kawit,_Cavite" title="Kawit, Cavite">
        Kawit
       </a>
       ). The officials of the pueblo were taken from the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Principal%C3%ADa" title="Principalía">
         Principalía
        </a>
       </i>
       , the noble class of pre-colonial origin. Their names are survived by prominent families in contemporary Philippine society such as Duremdes, Lindo, Tupas, Gatmaitan, Liwanag, Pangilinan, Panganiban, Balderas, and Agbayani, Apalisok, Aguinaldo to name a few.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Barrio_government">
        <i>
         Barrio
        </i>
        government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Barrio government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Barangay" title="Barangay">
        Barangay
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Every pueblo was further divided into "
       <i>
        barrio
       </i>
       s", and the
       <i>
        barrio
       </i>
       government (village or district) rested on the
       <i>
        barrio
       </i>
       administrator (
       <i>
        cabeza de barangay
       </i>
       ). He was responsible for peace and order and recruited men for
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:420px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Cebu.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="323" data-file-width="576" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Old_Cebu.jpg/418px-Old_Cebu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/10/Old_Cebu.jpg 1.5x" width="418"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Cebu.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Old view of a street in
         <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">
          Cebu
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       communal public works.
       <i>
        Cabezas
       </i>
       should be literate in Spanish and have good moral character and property. Cabezas who served for 25 years were exempted from forced labor.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition, this is where the sentiment heard as, "Mi Barrio", first came from.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Residencia_and_the_Visita">
        The
        <i>
         Residencia
        </i>
        and the
        <i>
         Visita
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The Residencia and the Visita">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       To check the abuse of power of royal officials, two ancient castilian institutions were brought to the Philippines. The
       <i>
        Residencia
       </i>
       , dating back to the 5th century and the
       <i>
        Visita
       </i>
       , which differed from the
       <i>
        residencia
       </i>
       in that it was conducted clandestinely by a
       <i>
        visitador-general
       </i>
       sent from Spain and might occur anytime within the official’s term, without any previous notice.
       <i>
        Visitas
       </i>
       may be specific or general.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Maura_law">
        Maura law
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Maura law">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The legal foundation for municipal governments in the country was laid with the promulgation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Maura_Law" title="Maura Law">
        Maura Law
       </a>
       on May 19, 1893. Named after its author,
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Maura" title="Antonio Maura">
        Don Antonio Maura
       </a>
       , the Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Colonies" title="Minister of the Colonies">
        Minister of Colonies
       </a>
       at the time, the law reorganized town governments in the Philippines with the aim of making them more effective and autonomous. This law created the municipal organization that was later adopted, revised, and further strengthened by the American and Filippino governments that succeeded Spanish.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Galleon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="300" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Spanish_Galleon.jpg/220px-Spanish_Galleon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Spanish_Galleon.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">
          Manila-Acapulco Trade
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:267px;">

          Malacañang Palace
         </a>
         was the seat of the colonial government of the Philippines
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">

         <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">

         ), Manila
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Manila-Acapulco_galleon_trade">
        Manila-Acapulco galleon trade
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Manila-Acapulco galleon trade">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleon" title="Manila Galleon">
        Manila-Acapulco Galleon Trade
       </a>
       was the main source of income for the colony during its early years. Service was inaugurated in 1565 and continued into the early 19th century. The Galleon trade brought
       <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">
        silver
       </a>
       from New Spain, which was used to purchase Asian goods such as
       <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">
        silk
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">
        spices
       </a>
       from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moluccas" title="Moluccas">
        Moluccas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lacquerware" title="Lacquerware">
        lacquerware
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       and Philippine
       <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">
        cotton
       </a>
       textiles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These goods were then exported to
       <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
        New Spain
       </a>
       and ultimately
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       by way of Manila. Thus, the Philippines earned its income through the trade of the Manila-Acapulco Galleon.
      </p>
      <p>
       The trade was established and operated primarily for the benefit of Spain and Spaniards. While the trade did bring some results which were beneficial to the Philippines, most effects were disadvantageous.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbl2002_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mbl2002-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the trade did result in cultural and commercial exchanges between Asia and the Americas that led to the introduction of new crops and animals to the Philippines such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">
        tamarind
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">
        avocado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">
        guava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">
        papaya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">
        pineapple
       </a>
       , horses and carabao.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbl2002_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mbl2002-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These gave the colony its first real income. The trade lasted for over two hundred years, and ceased in 1815 just before the secession of American colonies from Spain.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Society_of_Friends_of_the_Country">
        Royal Society of Friends of the Country
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Royal Society of Friends of the Country">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       José de Basco y Vargas, following a royal order to form a society of intellectuals who can produce new, useful ideas, formally established the Spanish Royal Economic Society of Friends of the Country, after the model of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Basque_Society_of_Friends_of_the_Country" title="Royal Basque Society of Friends of the Country">
        Royal Basque Society
       </a>
       . Composed of leading men in blocal and foreign scholarships and training grants in agriculture and established an academy of design. It was also credited to the carabao ban of 1782, the formation of the silversmiths and gold beaters guild and the construction of the first papermill in the Philippines in 1825. It was introduced in 1780, vanished temporarily in 1787-1819, 1820–1822 and 1875-1822 and ceased to exist in the middle of the 1890s.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Company_of_the_Philippines">
        Royal Company of the Philippines
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Royal Company of the Philippines">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Guipuzcoan_Company_of_Caracas" title="Guipuzcoan Company of Caracas">
        Guipuzcoan Company of Caracas
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On March 10, 1785,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Charles_III_of_Spain" title="King Charles III of Spain">
        King Charles III of Spain
       </a>
       confirmed the establishment of the Royal Philippine Company with a 25-year charter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After revocated the Royal Guipuzcoan Company of Caracas that had a monopoly on Venezuelan trade, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">
        Basque
       </a>
       -based company was granted a monopoly on the importation of Chinese and Indian goods into the Philippines, as well as the shipping of the goods directly to Spain via the
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">
        Cape of Good Hope
       </a>
       . The Dutch and British bitterly opposed them because they saw the company as a direct attack on their Asian trade. It also faced the hostility of the traders of the Galleon trade (see above) who saw it as competition. This gradually resulted in the death of both institutions: The Royal Philippine Company in 1814 and the Galleon trade in 1815.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first vessel of the Royal Philippine Company to set sail was the "Nuestra Señora de los Placeres" commanded by the captain Juan Antonio Zabaleta.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">
        Taxation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Taxation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Also there was the
       <i>
        bandalâ
       </i>
       (from the Tagalog word
       <i>
        mandalâ
       </i>
       , a round stack of rice stalks to be threshed), an annual forced sale and requisitioning of goods such as rice. Custom duties and income tax were also collected. By 1884, the tribute was replaced by the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cedula_personal" title="Cedula personal">
         cedula personal
        </a>
       </i>
       , wherein everyone over 18 were required to pay for personal identification.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The local
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gobernadorcillo" title="Gobernadorcillo">
         gobernadorcillos
        </a>
       </i>
       were responsible for collection of the tribute. Under the cedula system taxpayers were individually responsible to Spanish authorities for payment of the tax, and were subject to summary arrest for failure to show a cedula receipt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aside from paying a tribute, all male Filipinos from 16 to 60 years old were obliged to render forced labor called “polo”. This labor lasted for 40 days a year, later it was reduced to 15 days. It took various forms such as the building and repairing of roads and bridges, construction of Public buildings and churches, cutting timber in the forest, working in shipyards and serving as soldiers in military expeditions. People who rendered the forced labor was called “polistas”. He could be exempted by paying the “falla” which is a sum of money. The polista were according to law, to be given a daily rice ration during their working days which they often did not receive.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_attacks">
        Dutch attacks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dutch attacks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:446px;">
