        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_plaza_Moraga.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
          Manila
         </a>
         , capital of
         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
          Spanish East Indies
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:295px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="362" data-file-width="452" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg/293px-Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg/440px-Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="293"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Encarnacion_and_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The two merchant galleons—the
         <i>
          Encarnacion
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          Rosario
         </i>
         --which were hastily converted to warships to meet the superior Dutch armada of 18 vessels during the
         <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_La_Naval_de_Manila" title="Battles of La Naval de Manila">
          battles of La Naval de Manila
         </a>
         in 1646. (From an artist's conception)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1646, a series of five naval actions known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_La_Naval_de_Manila" title="Battles of La Naval de Manila">
        Battles of La Naval de Manila
       </a>
       was fought between the forces of Spain and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">
        Dutch Republic
       </a>
       , as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">
        Eighty Years' War
       </a>
       . Although the Spanish forces consisted of just two Manila galleons and a
       <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">
        galley
       </a>
       with crews composed mainly of Filipino volunteers, against three separate Dutch squadrons, totaling eighteen ships, the Dutch squadrons were severely defeated in all fronts by the Spanish-Filipino forces, forcing the Dutch to abandon their plans for an invasion of the Philippines.
      </p>
      <p>
       On June 6, 1647, Dutch vessels were sighted near Mariveles Island. In spite of the preparations, the Spanish had only one galleon (the
       <i>
        San Diego
       </i>
       ) and two galleys ready to engage the enemy. The Dutch had twelve major vessels.
      </p>
      <p>
       On June 12, the armada attacked the Spanish port of
       <a href="/wiki/Cavite_City" title="Cavite City">
        Cavite
       </a>
       . The battle lasted eight hours, and the Spanish believed they had done much damage to the enemy flagship and the other vessels. The Spanish ships were not badly damaged and casualties were low. However, nearly every roof in the Spanish settlement was damaged by cannon fire, which particularly concentrated on the cathedral. On June 19, the armada was split, with six ships sailing for the shipyard of
       <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">
        Mindoro
       </a>
       and the
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="381" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png/220px-Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png/330px-Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meztizo_Spanish_Woman.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Maria_Clara_gown" title="Maria Clara gown">
          Maria Clara gown
         </a>
         the Philippine national dress. was made during the colonial era by the Filipinos.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       other six remaining in
       <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">
        Manila Bay
       </a>
       . The Dutch next attacked
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       , where they captured the fortified monastery, taking prisoners and executing almost 200 Filipino defenders. The governor ordered solemn funeral rites for the dead and payments to their widows and orphans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recollect_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-recollect-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affairs_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-affairs-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reize_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-reize-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There was an expedition the following year that arrived in
       <a href="/wiki/Jolo" title="Jolo">
        Jolo
       </a>
       in July. The Dutch had formed an alliance with an anti-Spanish king, Salicala. The Spanish garrison on the island was small, but survived a Dutch bombardment. The Dutch finally withdrew, and the Spanish made peace with the Joloans, and then also withdrew.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recollect_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-recollect-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affairs_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-affairs-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reize_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-reize-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There was also an unsuccessful attack on
       <a href="/wiki/Zamboanga_(province)" title="Zamboanga (province)">
        Zamboanga
       </a>
       in 1648. That year the Dutch promised the natives of Mindanao that they would return in 1649 with aid in support of a revolt against the Spanish. Several revolts did break out, the most serious being in the village of Lindáo. There most of the Spaniards were killed, and the survivors were forced to flee in a small river boat to Butuán. However, Dutch aid did not materialize or have objects to provide them.The authorities from Manila issued a general pardon, and many of the Filipinos in the mountains surrendered. However, some of those were hung or they were enslaved.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recollect_28-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-recollect-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affairs_29-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-affairs-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reize_30-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-reize-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_invasion">
        British invasion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: British invasion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_of_Manila" title="British occupation of Manila">
        British occupation of Manila
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In August 1759, Charles III ascended the Spanish throne. At the time,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
        Britain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       were at war, in what was later
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:168px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude,_Manila_03.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg/166px-Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg/250px-Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg/333px-Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude%2C_Manila_03.jpg 2x" width="166"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Santiago_Postern_of_Our_Lady_of_Solitude,_Manila_03.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Postern of Our Lady of Solitude through which Governor General
         <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_de_Anda_y_Salazar" title="Simón de Anda y Salazar">
          Simón de Anda y Salazar
         </a>
         escaped with most government papers and about half the treasury.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       called the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
        Seven Years' War
       </a>
       . France, suffering a series of setbacks, successfully negotiated a treaty with Spain known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Family_Compact" title="Family Compact">
        Family Compact
       </a>
       which was signed on 15 August 1761. By an ancillary secret convention, Spain was committed to making preparations for war against Britain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholas_Tracy_1995,_p9_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nicholas_Tracy_1995,_p9-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The early success at Manila did not enable the British to control the Philippines. Spanish-Filipino forces (made up mostly of Filipinos) kept the British confined to Manila. Nevertheless, the British were confident of eventual success after receiving the written surrender of captured Catholic Archbishop Rojo on 30 October 1762.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholas_Tracy_1995,_p54_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nicholas_Tracy_1995,_p54-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The surrender was rejected as illegal by Don
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_de_Anda_y_Salazar" title="Simón de Anda y Salazar">
        Simón de Anda y Salazar
       </a>
       , who claimed the title of Governor-General under the statutes of the Council of Indies. He led Spanish-Filipino forces that kept the British confined to Manila and sabotaged or crushed British fomented revolts. Anda intercepted and redirected the Manila galleon trade to prevent further captures by the British. The failure of the British to consolidate their position led to troop desertions and a breakdown of command unity which left the British forces paralysed and in an increasingly precarious position.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Seven Years' War was ended by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">
        Peace of Paris
       </a>
       signed on 10 February 1763. At the time of signing the treaty, the signatories were not aware that the Manila was under British occupation and was being administered as a British colony. Consequently, no specific provision was made for the Philippines. Instead they fell under the general provision that all other lands not otherwise provided for be returned to the Spanish Crown.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Resistance_against_Spanish_rule">
        Resistance against Spanish rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Resistance against Spanish rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Spanish rule of the Philippines was constantly threatened by indigenous rebellions and invasions from the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">
        Dutch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_China" title="Greater China">
        Chinese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japanese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:381px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jaro_(Phil)_Reception-Taft.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1233" data-file-width="1830" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg/379px-Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg/569px-Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg/758px-Jaro_%28Phil%29_Reception-Taft.jpg 2x" width="379"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jaro_(Phil)_Reception-Taft.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Town of Jaro Philippines
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The previously dominant groups resisted Spanish rule, refusing to pay Spanish taxes and rejecting Spanish excesses. All were defeated by the Spanish and their Filipino allies. In many areas, the Spanish left indigenous groups to administer their own affairs but under Spanish overlordship.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_resistance">
        Early resistance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Early resistance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_revolts_against_Spain" title="Philippine revolts against Spain">
        Philippine revolts against Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish-Moro_Conflict" title="Spanish-Moro Conflict">
        Spanish-Moro Conflict
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Resistance against Spain did not immediately cease upon the conquest of the Austronesian cities. After
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rajah_patis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rajah patis (page does not exist)">
        Rajah patis
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">
        Cebu
       </a>
       , random native nobles resisted Spanish rule. The longest recorded native rebellion was that of
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Dagohoy" title="Francisco Dagohoy">
        Francisco Dagohoy
       </a>
       which lasted a century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the British occupation of Manila (1762–1764),
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Silang" title="Diego Silang">
        Diego Silang
       </a>
       was appointed by them as governor of
       <a href="/wiki/Ilocos" title="Ilocos">
        Ilocos
       </a>
       and after his assassination by fellow natives, his wife
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Silang" title="Gabriela Silang">
        Gabriela
       </a>
       continued to lead the Ilocanos in the fight against Spanish rule. Resistance against Spanish rule was regional in character, based on ethnolinguistic groups.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Hispanization did not spread to the mountainous center of northern Luzon, nor to the inland communities of Mindanao. The highlanders were more able to resist the Spanish invaders than the lowlanders.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_opening_of_the_Philippines_to_world_trade">
        The opening of the Philippines to world trade
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The opening of the Philippines to world trade">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:436px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="677" data-file-width="1236" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/434px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/651px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/868px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg 2x" width="434"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Old Photo of
         <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
          Manila
         </a>
         's streets with
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahay_na_Bato" title="Bahay na Bato">
          Bahay na Bato
         </a>
         edifices and
         <a href="/wiki/Kalesa" title="Kalesa">
          Kalesa
         </a>
         . A Filipino architecture and transportation made during the Spanish era.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       spread from
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
        Great Britain
       </a>
       during the period known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victorian_Age" title="Victorian Age">
        Victorian Age
       </a>
       . The industrialization of Europe
      </p>
      <p>
       created great demands for raw materials from the colonies, bringing with it investment and wealth, although this was very unevenly distributed. Governor-General
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Basco_y_Vargas" title="José Basco y Vargas">
        Basco
       </a>
       had opened the Philippines to this trade. Previously, the Philippines was seen as a trading post for international trade but in the nineteenth century it was developed both as a source of raw materials and as a market for manufactured goods. The economy of the Philippines rose rapidly and its local industries developed to satisfy the rising demands of an industrializing Europe. A small flow of European immigrants came with the opening of the
       <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
        Suez Canal
       </a>
       , which cut the travel time between Europe and the Philippines by half. New ideas about government and society, which the friars and colonial authorities found dangerous, quickly found their way into the Philippines, notably through the
       <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">
        Freemasons
       </a>
       , who along with others, spread the ideals of the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
        American
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French
       </a>
       and other revolutions, including
       <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_and_radicalism_in_Spain" title="Liberalism and radicalism in Spain">
        Spanish liberalism
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Filipino_nationalism">
        Rise of Filipino nationalism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rise of Filipino nationalism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Filipino_nationalism" title="Filipino nationalism">
        Filipino nationalism
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:186px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Filipino_mestizo_couple,_early_1800s.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="583" data-file-width="552" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg/184px-Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg/275px-Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg/367px-Filipino_mestizo_couple%2C_early_1800s.jpg 2x" width="184"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Filipino_mestizo_couple,_early_1800s.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tagalog Filipino mestizo, early 1800s. Original caption: Métis indiens-espagnols. From
         <i>
          Aventures d'un Gentilhomme Breton aux iles Philippines
         </i>
         by Paul de la Gironiere, published in 1855.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:396px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="950" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg/394px-La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg/591px-La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg/788px-La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg 2x" width="394"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Insular_Cigar_Factory_Manila.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The opening of Philippine trade to the world gave rise to business and beautiful edifices that made Manila the Paris of Asia. La Insular Cigar Factory is one of the most popular.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The development of the Philippines as a source of raw materials and as a market for European manufactures created much local wealth. Many Filipinos prospered. Everyday Filipinos also benefited from the new economy with the rapid increase in demand for labor and availability of business opportunities. Some Europeans immigrated to the Philippines to join the wealth wagon, among them Jacobo Zobel, patriarch of today's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zobel_de_Ayala_family" title="Zobel de Ayala family">
        Zobel de Ayala family
       </a>
       and prominent figure in the rise of Filipino nationalism. Their scions studied in the best universities of Europe where they learned the ideals of liberty from the French and American Revolutions. The new economy gave rise to a new middle class in the Philippines, usually not ethnic Filipinos.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="892" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/220px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/330px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/440px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Manila_Cathedral" title="Manila Cathedral">
          Manila Cathedral
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the mid-19th century, the Suez Canal was opened which made the Philippines easier to reach from Spain. The small increase of
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peninsulares" title="Peninsulares">
         Peninsulares
        </a>
       </i>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       threatened the secularization of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Philippines" title="Roman Catholicism in the Philippines">
        Philippine churches
       </a>
       . In state affairs, the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criollo_(people)" title="Criollo (people)">
         Criollos
        </a>
       </i>
       , known locally as
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       (lit. "islanders"). were displaced from government positions by the
       <i>
        Peninsulares
       </i>
       , whom the native
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       regarded as foreigners. The
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       had become increasingly Filipino and called themselves
       <i>
        Los hijos del país
       </i>
       (lit. "sons of the country"). Among the early proponents of Filipino nationalism were the
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       Padre
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Pel%C3%A1ez" title="Pedro Peláez">
        Pedro Peláez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Manila" title="Archbishop of Manila">
        archbishop of Manila
       </a>
       , who fought for the secularization of Philippine churches and expulsion of the friars; Padre
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Burgos" title="José Burgos">
        José Burgos
       </a>
       whose execution influenced the national hero
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">
        José Rizal
       </a>
       ; and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joaqu%C3%ADn_Pardo_de_Tavera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joaquín Pardo de Tavera (page does not exist)">
        Joaquín Pardo de Tavera
       </a>
       who fought for retention of government positions by natives, regardless of race. In retaliation to the rise of Filipino nationalism, the friars called the
       <i>
        Indios
       </i>
       (possibly referring to
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Filipino_mestizo" title="Filipino mestizo">
         mestizos
        </a>
       </i>
       as well) indolent and unfit for government and church positions. In response, the
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       came out with
       <i>
        Indios agraviados
       </i>
       , a manifesto defending the Filipino against discriminatory remarks. The tension between the
       <i>
        Insulares
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Peninsulares
       </i>
       erupted into the failed revolts of
       <a href="/wiki/Novales" title="Novales">
        Novales
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cavite_Mutiny" title="Cavite Mutiny">
        Cavite Mutiny
       </a>
       of 1872 which resulted to the deportation of prominent Filipino nationalists to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marianas" title="Marianas">
        Marianas
       </a>
       and Europe who would continue the fight for liberty through the Propaganda Movement. The Cavite Mutiny implicated the priests
       <a href="/wiki/Mariano_G%C3%B3mez" title="Mariano Gómez">
        Mariano Gómez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Burgos" title="José Burgos">
        José Burgos
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Jacinto_Zamora" title="Jacinto Zamora">
        Jacinto Zamora
       </a>
       (see
       <a href="/wiki/Gomburza" title="Gomburza">
        Gomburza
       </a>
       ) whose executions would influence the subversive activities of the next generation of Filipino nationalists, José Rizal, who then dedicated his novel,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_filibusterismo" title="El filibusterismo">
         El filibusterismo
        </a>
       </i>
       to these priests.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="369" data-file-width="550" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg/346px-San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg/519px-San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg 2x" width="346"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San-Juan-de-Letran.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Colegio San Juan de Letran,
         <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">
          Intramuros
         </a>
         Manila (ca. 1880)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Spanish_liberalism">
        Rise of Spanish liberalism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rise of Spanish liberalism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_and_radicalism_in_Spain" title="Liberalism and radicalism in Spain">
        Liberalism and radicalism in Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the Liberals won the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Revolution_of_1868" title="Spanish Revolution of 1868">
        Spanish Revolution of 1868
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Mar%C3%ADa_de_la_Torre_y_Nava_Cerrada" title="Carlos María de la Torre y Nava Cerrada">
        Carlos María de la Torre
       </a>
       was sent to the Philippines to serve as governor-general (1869–1871). He was one of the most loved governors-general in the Philippines because of the reforms he implemented.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       At one time, his supporters, including Padre Burgos and Joaquín Pardo de Tavera, serenaded him in front of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1an_Palace" title="Malacañan Palace">
        Malacañan Palace
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Following the Bourbon Restoration in Spain and the removal of the Liberals from power, de la Torre was recalled and replaced by Governor-General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rafael_de_Izquierdo_y_Gut%C3%ADerrez" title="Rafael de Izquierdo y Gutíerrez">
        Izquierdo
       </a>
       who vowed to rule with an iron fist.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Freemasonry">
        Freemasonry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Freemasonry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="670" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg/220px-Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg/330px-Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg/440px-Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Filipino_Ilustrados_Jose_Rizal_Marcelo_del_Pilar_Mariano_Ponce.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">
          José Rizal
         </a>
         (Left) the Filipino national hero
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">
        Freemasonry
       </a>
       had gained a generous following in Europe and the Americas during the 19th century and found its way to the Philippines. The
      </p>
      <p>
       Western World was quickly changing and sought less political control from the Roman Catholic Church.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first Filipino Masonic lodge was
       <i>
        Revoluccion
       </i>
       . It was established by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graciano_Lopez_Jaena" title="Graciano Lopez Jaena">
        Graciano Lopez Jaena
       </a>
       in Barcelona and was recognized in April 1889. It did not last long after he resigned from being its worshipful master on November 29, 1889.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1889,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_H._del_Pilar" title="Marcelo H. del Pilar">
        Marcelo H. del Pilar
       </a>
       established, with the help of Julio Llorente, the
       <i>
        Solidaridad
       </i>
       in Madrid. Its first worshipful master was Llorente. A short time later, the
       <i>
        Solidaridad
       </i>
       grew. Some its members included
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">
        José Rizal
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pedro_Serrano_Laktaw&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pedro Serrano Laktaw (page does not exist)">
        Pedro Serrano Laktaw
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Baldomero_Roxas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Baldomero Roxas (page does not exist)">
        Baldomero Roxas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Galicano_Apacible" title="Galicano Apacible">
        Galicano Apacible
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1891, Del Pilar sent Laktaw to the Philippines to establish a Masonic lodge. Laktaw established on January 6, 1892, the
       <i>
        Nilad
       </i>
       , the first Masonic lodge in the Philippines. It is estimated that there were 35 masonic lodges in the Philippines in 1893 of which nine were in Manila. The first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipina" title="Filipina">
        Filipina
       </a>
       freemason was
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario_Villaruel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rosario Villaruel (page does not exist)">
        Rosario Villaruel
       </a>
       . Trinidad and Josefa Rizal,
       <a href="/wiki/Marina_Dizon" title="Marina Dizon">
        Marina Dizon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Romualda_Lanuza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Romualda Lanuza (page does not exist)">
        Romualda Lanuza
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Purificacion_Leyva&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Purificacion Leyva (page does not exist)">
        Purificacion Leyva
       </a>
       , and many others join the masonic lodge.
      </p>
      <p>
       Freemasonry was important during the time of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">
        Philippine Revolution
       </a>
       . It pushed the reform movement and carried out the propaganda work. In the Philippines, many of those who pushed for a revolution were member of freemasonry like
       <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio" title="Andrés Bonifacio">
        Andrés Bonifacio
       </a>
       . In fact, the organization used by Bonifacio in establishing the
       <a href="/wiki/Katipunan" title="Katipunan">
        Katipunan
       </a>
       was derived from the Masonic society. It may be said that joining masonry was one activity that both the reformists and the Katipuneros shared.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Illustrados.2C_Rizal_and_Katipunan">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Illustrados,_Rizal_and_Katipunan">
        Illustrados, Rizal and Katipunan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Illustrados, Rizal and Katipunan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Liga.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="680" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/La_Liga.jpg/250px-La_Liga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/La_Liga.jpg/375px-La_Liga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/La_Liga.jpg/500px-La_Liga.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Liga.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Filipino
         <i>
          Ilustrados
         </i>
         in Spain.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:273px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katipuneros.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1163" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Katipuneros.jpg/271px-Katipuneros.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Katipuneros.jpg/407px-Katipuneros.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Katipuneros.jpg/542px-Katipuneros.jpg 2x" width="271"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katipuneros.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Katipuneros
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The mass deportation of nationalists to the Marianas and Europe in 1872 led to a Filipino expatriate community of reformers in Europe. The community grew with the next generation of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilustrados" title="Ilustrados">
        Ilustrados
       </a>
       studying in European universities. They allied themselves with Spanish liberals, notably Spanish senator
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Morayta_Sagrario&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miguel Morayta Sagrario (page does not exist)">
        Miguel Morayta Sagrario
       </a>
       , and founded the newspaper
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Solidaridad" title="La Solidaridad">
         La Solidaridad
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the reformers was
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">
        José Rizal
       </a>
       , who wrote two novels while in Europe. His novels were considered
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (August 2013)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the most influential of the Illustrados' writings causing further unrest in the islands, particularly the founding of the
       <a href="/wiki/Katipunan" title="Katipunan">
        Katipunan
       </a>
       . A rivalry developed between himself and
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_H._del_Pilar" title="Marcelo H. del Pilar">
        Marcelo H. del Pilar
       </a>
       for the leadership of
       <i>
        La Solidaridad
       </i>
       and the reform movement in Europe. Majority of the expatriates supported the leadership of del Pilar.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gat_Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="225" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Gat_Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio.jpg/220px-Gat_Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e6/Gat_Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gat_Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bonifacio" title="Andrés Bonifacio">
          Andrés Bonifacio
         </a>
         , Father of the
         <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">
          Philippine Revolution
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rizal then returned to the Philippines to organize
       <a href="/wiki/La_Liga_Filipina" title="La Liga Filipina">
        La Liga Filipina
       </a>
       and bring the reform movement to Philippine soil. He was arrested just a few days after founding the league. In 1892, Radical members of the La Liga Filipina, which included Bonifacio and
       <a href="/wiki/Deodato_Arellano" title="Deodato Arellano">
        Deodato Arellano
       </a>
       , founded the
       <i>
        Kataastaasan Kagalanggalang Katipunan ng mga Anak ng Bayan
       </i>
       (KKK), called simply the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Katipunan" title="Katipunan">
         Katipunan
        </a>
       </i>
       , which had the objective of the Philippines seceding from the Spanish Empire.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Philippine_Revolution">
        The Philippine Revolution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The Philippine Revolution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">
        Philippine Revolution
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_(ca._1898).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="303" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg/250px-Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg 1.5x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_(ca._1898).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">
          Emilio Aguinaldo
         </a>
         , The first Philippine President
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By 1896 the Katipunan had a membership by the thousands. That same year, the existence of the Katipunan was discovered by the colonial authorities. In late August Katipuneros gathered in Caloocan and declared the start of the revolution. The event is now known as the Cry of Balintawak or Cry of Pugad Lawin, due to conflicting historical traditions and official government positions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agoncillop166_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-agoncillop166-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Andrés Bonifacio called for a general offensive on Manila
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was defeated in battle at the town of San Juan del Monte. He regrouped his forces and was able to briefly capture the towns of Marikina, San Mateo and Montalban. Spanish counterattacks drove him back and he retreated to the mountains of Balara and Morong and from there engaged in
       <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">
        guerrilla warfare
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guerreropp175-176_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guerreropp175-176-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By August 30, the revolt had spread to eight provinces. On that date, Governor-General Ramon Blanco declared a
       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">
        state of war
       </a>
       in these provinces and placed them under
       <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">
        martial law
       </a>
       . These were
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bulacan" title="Bulacan">
        Bulacan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cavite" title="Cavite">
        Cavite
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tarlac" title="Tarlac">
        Tarlac
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Laguna_(province)" title="Laguna (province)">
        Laguna
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Batangas" title="Batangas">
        Batangas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Ecija" title="Nueva Ecija">
        Nueva Ecija
       </a>
       . They would later be represented in the eight rays of the sun in the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Philippines" title="Flag of the Philippines">
        Filipino flag
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agoncillop173_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Agoncillop173-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="Look at en:History of the Philippines (1521–1898)&amp;diff=prev&amp;oldid=306597158, which initially added this; the source does not support that assertion either (at least not on the cited page). Filipino historians today disagree about naming the eight provinces. If the eight provinces are to be named, the discgreement about their naming should be clarified. (October 2011)">
           not in citation given
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Emilio Aguinaldo and the Katipuneros of Cavite were the most successful of the rebels
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and they controlled most of their province by September–October. They defended their territories with
       <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">
        trenches
       </a>
       designed by
       <a href="/wiki/Edilberto_Evangelista" title="Edilberto Evangelista">
        Edilberto Evangelista
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guerreropp175-176_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-guerreropp175-176-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:311px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg/309px-IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg/464px-IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg/618px-IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg 2x" width="309"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IJVMarcelAgoncillo4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Marcela_Agoncillo" title="Marcela Agoncillo">
          Marcela Agoncillo
         </a>
         (center), principal seamstress of the first official flag of the Philippines.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many of the educated
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ilustrado" title="Ilustrado">
         ilustrado
        </a>
       </i>
       class such as
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Luna" title="Antonio Luna">
        Antonio Luna
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Apolinario_Mabini" title="Apolinario Mabini">
        Apolinario Mabini
       </a>
       did not initially favor an armed revolution. Rizal himself, whom the rebels took inspiration from and had consulted beforehand, disapproved of a premature revolution. He was arrested, tried and executed for treason, sedition and conspiracy on December 30, 1896. Before his arrest he had issued a statement disavowing the revolution, but in his
       <a href="/wiki/Swan_song" title="Swan song">
        swan song
       </a>
       poem
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mi_%C3%BAltimo_adi%C3%B3s" title="Mi último adiós">
         Mi último adiós
        </a>
       </i>
       he wrote that dying in battle for the sake of one's country was just as patriotic as his own impending death.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quibuyen_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-quibuyen-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (August 2011)">
           page needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While the revolution spread throughout the provinces, Aguinaldo's Katipuneros declared the existence of an insurgent government in October regardless of Bonifacio's Katipunan,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constantinop178-181_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-constantinop178-181-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which he had already converted into an insurgent government with him as president in August.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guerreropp166-167_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guerreropp166-167-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bonifacio was invited to Cavite to mediate between Aguinaldo's rebels, the
       <a href="/wiki/Magdalo_(Katipunan_faction)" title="Magdalo (Katipunan faction)">
        Magdalo
       </a>
       , and their rivals the
       <a href="/wiki/Magdiwang_(Katipunan_faction)" title="Magdiwang (Katipunan faction)">
        Magdiwang
       </a>
       , both chapters of the Katipunan. There he became embroiled in discussions whether to replace the Katipunan with an insurgent government of the Cavite rebels' design. To this end, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tejeros_Convention" title="Tejeros Convention">
        Tejeros Convention
       </a>
       was convened, where Aguinaldo was elected president of the new insurgent government. Bonifacio refused to recognize this and he was executed for treason in May 1897.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agoncillopp180-181_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-agoncillopp180-181-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By December 1897, the revolution had resulted to a stalemate between the colonial government and rebels. Pedro Paterno mediated between the two sides for the signing of the Pact of Biak-na-Bato. The conditions of the armistice included the self-exile of Aguinaldo and his officers in exchange for $800,000 or 40,104,392.82542 pesosto be paid by the colonial government. Aguinaldo then sailed to
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       for self exile.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="The_Spanish.E2.80.93American_War">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Spanish–American_War">
        The Spanish–American War
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Spanish–American War">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">
        Philippine–American War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite,_Luz%C3%B3n,_Filipinas.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg/330px-Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg/495px-Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg/660px-Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite%2C_Luz%C3%B3n%2C_Filipinas.jpg 2x" width="330"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casa_del_general_Aguinaldo_en_Cavite,_Luz%C3%B3n,_Filipinas.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Aguinaldo_Shrine" title="Aguinaldo Shrine">
          House of Emilio Aguinaldo
         </a>
         is where the proclamation of Philippine Independence from Spain took place on June 12, 1898.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On April 25, 1898, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       began. On May 1, 1898, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">
        Battle of Manila Bay
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_Squadron" title="Asiatic Squadron">
        Asiatic Squadron
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">
        U.S. Navy
       </a>
       , led by Commodore
       <a href="/wiki/George_Dewey" title="George Dewey">
        George Dewey
       </a>
       aboard the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/USS_Olympia_(C-6)" title="USS Olympia (C-6)">
         USS Olympia
        </a>
       </i>
       , decisively defeated the Spanish naval forces in the Philippines. With the loss of its naval forces and of control of Manila Bay, Spain lost the ability to defend Manila and therefore the Philippines.
      </p>
      <p>
       On May 19, Emilio Aguinaldo returned to the Philippines aboard a U.S. Navy ship and on May 24 took command of Filipino forces. Filipino forces had liberated much of the country from the Spanish.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       On June 12, 1898 Aguinaldo issued the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Philippine Declaration of Independence">
        Philippine Declaration of Independence
       </a>
       declaring independence from Spain. Filipino forces then laid siege to Manila, as had American forces.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:210px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="740" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/208px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/312px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/416px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg 2x" width="208"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">
          Battle of Manila Bay
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In August 1898, the Spanish governor-general covertly agreed with American commanders to surrender Manila to the Americans following a mock battle. On August 13, 1898, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila (1898)">
        Battle of Manila (1898)
       </a>
       , Americans took control of the city. In December, 1898, the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">
        Treaty of Paris (1898)
       </a>
       was signed, ending the Spanish–American War and selling the Philippines to the United States for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Dollar" title="United States Dollar">
        $
       </a>
       20 million. With this treaty, Spanish rule in the Philippines formally ended.
      </p>
      <p>
       On January 23, 1899, Aguinaldo established the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic" title="First Philippine Republic">
        First Philippine Republic
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Malolos" title="Malolos">
        Malolos
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 4, 1899, the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">
        Philippine–American War
       </a>
       began with the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1899)" title="Battle of Manila (1899)">
        Battle of Manila (1899)
       </a>
       between Americans forces and the nascent Philippine Republic.
      </p>
      <h2>

         <span class="reference-text">

           </a>

          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Spanish+Expeditions+to+the+Philippines&amp;rft.pub=PHILIPPINE-HISTORY.ORG&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.philippine-history.org%2Fspanish-expeditions.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHistory+of+the+Philippines+%281521%E2%80%931898%29">

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

           <a href="#cite_ref-11">

           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.livinginthephilippines.com/travel-guides/getting-to-philippines/979-tourist-attraction-city-of-manila" rel="nofollow">
            "Living in the Philippines: Living, Retiring, Travelling and Doing Business"
           </a>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Living+in+the+Philippines%3A+Living%2C+Retiring%2C+Travelling+and+Doing+Business&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.livinginthephilippines.com%2Ftravel-guides%2Fgetting-to-philippines%2F979-tourist-attraction-city-of-manila&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHistory+of+the+Philippines+%281521%E2%80%931898%29">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-12">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-12">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation journal">
           Barrows, David (2014).
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/38269/38269-h/38269-h.htm#pb139" rel="nofollow">
            "A History of the Philippines"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            Guttenburg Free Online E-books
           </i>
           .
           <b>
            1
           </b>
           : 229.
           <q>
            Reforms under General Arandía.—The demoralization and misery with which Obando's rule closed were relieved somewhat by the capable government of Arandía, who succeeded him. Arandía was one of the few men of talent, energy, and integrity who stood at the head of affairs in these islands during two centuries. He reformed the greatly disorganized military force, establishing what was known as the "Regiment of the King,"
            <b>
             made up very largely of Mexican soldiers
            </b>
            . He also formed a corps of artillerists composed of Filipinos. These were regular troops, who received from Arandía sufficient pay to enable them to live decently and like an army.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Guttenburg+Free+Online+E-books&amp;rft.atitle=A+History+of+the+Philippines&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.pages=229&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.aulast=Barrows&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gutenberg.org%2Ffiles%2F38269%2F38269-h%2F38269-h.htm%23pb139&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHistory+of+the+Philippines+%281521%E2%80%931898%29">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-13">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         <span class="reference-text">

          </a>
          (Zamboanga City History) "He (Governor Don Sebastían Hurtado de Corcuera) brought a great reënforcements of soldiers, many of them from
          <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">

          </a>
          , as he made his voyage to
